<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="91b1a281c683456c9a98966c1f0a90b1"><span data-offset-key="91b1a281c683456c9a98966c1f0a90b1:0">Copying and Pasting Strings with the pyperclip Module (need pip install)</span></span></span>

    >>> import pyperclip​>>> pyperclip.copy('Hello world!')​>>> pyperclip.paste()'Hello world!'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a1fc7d56d45f4a528e176cb15b029956"><span data-offset-key="a1fc7d56d45f4a528e176cb15b029956:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="59304f3696e84283aa2a74432f88dbbe"><span data-offset-key="59304f3696e84283aa2a74432f88dbbe:0">String Formatting</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="327dea0b13f24646bf9dfc5d7f6f1c72"><span data-offset-key="327dea0b13f24646bf9dfc5d7f6f1c72:0">% operator</span></span></span>

    >>> name = 'Pete'>>> 'Hello %s' % name"Hello Pete"

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="768aa96c40bb4afbbd5fa69b1017e26e"><span data-offset-key="768aa96c40bb4afbbd5fa69b1017e26e:0">We can use the </span><span data-offset-key="768aa96c40bb4afbbd5fa69b1017e26e:1">`%x`</span><span data-offset-key="768aa96c40bb4afbbd5fa69b1017e26e:2"> format specifier to convert an int value to a string:</span></span></span>

    >>> num = 5>>> 'I have %x apples' % num"I have 5 apples"

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="88ecb24fe1c844488ff519704369dfe8"><span data-offset-key="88ecb24fe1c844488ff519704369dfe8:0">Note: For new code, using str.format or f-strings (Python 3.6+) is strongly recommended over the </span><span data-offset-key="88ecb24fe1c844488ff519704369dfe8:1">`%`</span><span data-offset-key="88ecb24fe1c844488ff519704369dfe8:2"> operator.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3432ee0cc8864efcb105d5fe36a98563"><span data-offset-key="3432ee0cc8864efcb105d5fe36a98563:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4c744204885c44dfb2062c3add2771c7"><span data-offset-key="4c744204885c44dfb2062c3add2771c7:0">String Formatting (str.format)</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="51443416064540b2890e6658056d434f"><span data-offset-key="51443416064540b2890e6658056d434f:0">Python 3 introduced a new way to do string formatting that was later back-ported to Python 2.7. This makes the syntax for string formatting more regular.</span></span></span>

    >>> name = 'John'>>> age = 20'​>>> "Hello I'm {}, my age is {}".format(name, age)"Hello I'm John, my age is 20"

    >>> "Hello I'm {0}, my age is {1}".format(name, age)"Hello I'm John, my age is 20"

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e48f278dde6947b8bb09a0baf0df66ab"><span data-offset-key="e48f278dde6947b8bb09a0baf0df66ab:0">The official </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/stdtypes.html?highlight=sprintf#printf-style-string-formatting" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="1cef7039e35e4153b7e5eb12faef812c"><span data-offset-key="1cef7039e35e4153b7e5eb12faef812c:0">Python 3.x documentation</span></span></a><span data-key="8f2c6143658d4574a3dd83981c7afb4b"><span data-offset-key="8f2c6143658d4574a3dd83981c7afb4b:0"> recommend </span><span data-offset-key="8f2c6143658d4574a3dd83981c7afb4b:1">`str.format`</span><span data-offset-key="8f2c6143658d4574a3dd83981c7afb4b:2"> over the </span><span data-offset-key="8f2c6143658d4574a3dd83981c7afb4b:3">`%`</span><span data-offset-key="8f2c6143658d4574a3dd83981c7afb4b:4"> operator:</span></span></span>

> <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a00c4c01bc584a3aa1265287ae465f94"><span data-offset-key="a00c4c01bc584a3aa1265287ae465f94:0">The formatting operations described here exhibit a variety of quirks that lead to a number of common errors (such as failing to display tuples and dictionaries correctly). Using the newer formatted string literals or the str.format() interface helps avoid these errors. These alternatives also provide more powerful, flexible and extensible approaches to formatting text.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7d1d28894f414811b9a0ccd5f92119df"><span data-offset-key="7d1d28894f414811b9a0ccd5f92119df:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6dfb22b5607c4af099adb3f9d7e7d9b3"><span data-offset-key="6dfb22b5607c4af099adb3f9d7e7d9b3:0">Lazy string formatting</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="38ca0501cab44b6e8eb14af08b20567e"><span data-offset-key="38ca0501cab44b6e8eb14af08b20567e:0">You would only use </span><span data-offset-key="38ca0501cab44b6e8eb14af08b20567e:1">`%s`</span><span data-offset-key="38ca0501cab44b6e8eb14af08b20567e:2"> string formatting on functions that can do lazy parameters evaluation, the most common being logging:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1098b46500944edc99307b2f72e391ae"><span data-offset-key="1098b46500944edc99307b2f72e391ae:0">Prefer:</span></span></span>

    >>> name = "alice">>> logging.debug("User name: %s", name)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="847d4a51b4314ecca14ba1e83c5ccf20"><span data-offset-key="847d4a51b4314ecca14ba1e83c5ccf20:0">Over:</span></span></span>

    >>> logging.debug("User name: {}".format(name))

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e532b305ba4c4b888f33f8d4ce2478e9"><span data-offset-key="e532b305ba4c4b888f33f8d4ce2478e9:0">Or:</span></span></span>

    >>> logging.debug("User name: " + name)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="96d2ce4a6ad24a32ab394f89e0c8d080"><span data-offset-key="96d2ce4a6ad24a32ab394f89e0c8d080:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d33c3c86135e42ecbb5fe127db435a08"><span data-offset-key="d33c3c86135e42ecbb5fe127db435a08:0">Formatted String Literals or f-strings (Python 3.6+)</span></span></span>

    >>> name = 'Elizabeth'>>> f'Hello {name}!''Hello Elizabeth!

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f505ed7a95b24cb09490c62f81cf028c"><span data-offset-key="f505ed7a95b24cb09490c62f81cf028c:0">It is even possible to do inline arithmetic with it:</span></span></span>

    >>> a = 5>>> b = 10>>> f'Five plus ten is {a + b} and not {2 * (a + b)}.''Five plus ten is 15 and not 30.'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="939b1a04172d4cd98f143ce2346a3b3a"><span data-offset-key="939b1a04172d4cd98f143ce2346a3b3a:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="01e3270ea4154ee6ac896ea026b22c72"><span data-offset-key="01e3270ea4154ee6ac896ea026b22c72:0">Template Strings</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="096de43b67c74f0085c2d3f8be7ea8a1"><span data-offset-key="096de43b67c74f0085c2d3f8be7ea8a1:0">A simpler and less powerful mechanism, but it is recommended when handling format strings generated by users. Due to their reduced complexity template strings are a safer choice.</span></span></span>

    >>> from string import Template>>> name = 'Elizabeth'>>> t = Template('Hey $name!')>>> t.substitute(name=name)'Hey Elizabeth!'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="050ccfe5142d41e4945f5b5c0891b36e"><span data-offset-key="050ccfe5142d41e4945f5b5c0891b36e:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="04167c56cc944ea4b4800cc96ec41eea"><span data-offset-key="04167c56cc944ea4b4800cc96ec41eea:0">Regular Expressions</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7c3df7cf4f2b4748adef82bd069d0bee"><span data-offset-key="7c3df7cf4f2b4748adef82bd069d0bee:0">Import the regex module with </span><span data-offset-key="7c3df7cf4f2b4748adef82bd069d0bee:1">`import re`</span><span data-offset-key="7c3df7cf4f2b4748adef82bd069d0bee:2">.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a8c9c913a95147f891efc2fafed1ccaa"><span data-offset-key="a8c9c913a95147f891efc2fafed1ccaa:0">Create a Regex object with the </span><span data-offset-key="a8c9c913a95147f891efc2fafed1ccaa:1">`re.compile()`</span><span data-offset-key="a8c9c913a95147f891efc2fafed1ccaa:2"> function. (Remember to use a raw string.)</span></span></span>

3.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="80ea325cb2ea40f7aea05e5247aef1df"><span data-offset-key="80ea325cb2ea40f7aea05e5247aef1df:0">Pass the string you want to search into the Regex object’s </span><span data-offset-key="80ea325cb2ea40f7aea05e5247aef1df:1">`search()`</span><span data-offset-key="80ea325cb2ea40f7aea05e5247aef1df:2"> method. This returns a </span><span data-offset-key="80ea325cb2ea40f7aea05e5247aef1df:3">`Match`</span><span data-offset-key="80ea325cb2ea40f7aea05e5247aef1df:4"> object.</span></span></span>

4.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1d390806b71a42d68624a57b594987c8"><span data-offset-key="1d390806b71a42d68624a57b594987c8:0">Call the Match object’s </span><span data-offset-key="1d390806b71a42d68624a57b594987c8:1">`group()`</span><span data-offset-key="1d390806b71a42d68624a57b594987c8:2"> method to return a string of the actual matched text.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2be2de42799a40c28ea69f90f26da842"><span data-offset-key="2be2de42799a40c28ea69f90f26da842:0">All the regex functions in Python are in the re module:</span></span></span>

    >>> import re

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e66d886757d640fb8b286ca23d9e0a7b"><span data-offset-key="e66d886757d640fb8b286ca23d9e0a7b:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c499af2f66734efa82a126811016d2c0"><span data-offset-key="c499af2f66734efa82a126811016d2c0:0">Matching Regex Objects</span></span></span>

    >>> phone_num_regex = re.compile(r'\d\d\d-\d\d\d-\d\d\d\d')​>>> mo = phone_num_regex.search('My number is 415-555-4242.')​>>> print('Phone number found: {}'.format(mo.group()))Phone number found: 415-555-4242

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c50cac476dbb449d93f5681d9d411050"><span data-offset-key="c50cac476dbb449d93f5681d9d411050:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="642cf05233c04433b0a06c6ceeffdd4b"><span data-offset-key="642cf05233c04433b0a06c6ceeffdd4b:0">Grouping with Parentheses</span></span></span>

    >>> phone_num_regex = re.compile(r'(\d\d\d)-(\d\d\d-\d\d\d\d)')​>>> mo = phone_num_regex.search('My number is 415-555-4242.')​>>> mo.group(1)'415'​>>> mo.group(2)'555-4242'​>>> mo.group(0)'415-555-4242'​>>> mo.group()'415-555-4242'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b52c97948c134a10a6162ccdd28767a8"><span data-offset-key="b52c97948c134a10a6162ccdd28767a8:0">To retrieve all the groups at once: use the groups() method—note the plural form for the name.</span></span></span>

    >>> mo.groups()('415', '555-4242')​>>> area_code, main_number = mo.groups()​>>> print(area_code)415​>>> print(main_number)555-4242

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b3c3b5763ecf4fcca924a9e7e1778515"><span data-offset-key="b3c3b5763ecf4fcca924a9e7e1778515:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="223269c5668e413997a8072ce904a5f2"><span data-offset-key="223269c5668e413997a8072ce904a5f2:0">Matching Multiple Groups with the Pipe</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="24310347bfa546f1a8cbc46910eeb73e"><span data-offset-key="24310347bfa546f1a8cbc46910eeb73e:0">The | character is called a pipe. You can use it anywhere you want to match one of many expressions. For example, the regular expression r'Batman|Tina Fey' will match either 'Batman' or 'Tina Fey'.</span></span></span>

    >>> hero_regex = re.compile (r'Batman|Tina Fey')​>>> mo1 = hero_regex.search('Batman and Tina Fey.')​>>> mo1.group()'Batman'​>>> mo2 = hero_regex.search('Tina Fey and Batman.')​>>> mo2.group()'Tina Fey'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5d889c7e2b5d43288f7d7b6add07f7db"><span data-offset-key="5d889c7e2b5d43288f7d7b6add07f7db:0">You can also use the pipe to match one of several patterns as part of your regex:</span></span></span>

    >>> bat_regex = re.compile(r'Bat(man|mobile|copter|bat)')​>>> mo = bat_regex.search('Batmobile lost a wheel')​>>> mo.group()'Batmobile'​>>> mo.group(1)'mobile'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9fb198dba8df48a7af38d3027b87d5f8"><span data-offset-key="9fb198dba8df48a7af38d3027b87d5f8:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c27a0bf9ef02498eae7a61c774d97b98"><span data-offset-key="c27a0bf9ef02498eae7a61c774d97b98:0">Optional Matching with the Question Mark</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a79267a847e341808951a7da899f0244"><span data-offset-key="a79267a847e341808951a7da899f0244:0">The ? character flags the group that precedes it as an optional part of the pattern.</span></span></span>

    >>> bat_regex = re.compile(r'Bat(wo)?man')>>> mo1 = bat_regex.search('The Adventures of Batman')>>> mo1.group()'Batman'​>>> mo2 = bat_regex.search('The Adventures of Batwoman')>>> mo2.group()'Batwoman'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0192be4220884c8c9d54b4a139731cd1"><span data-offset-key="0192be4220884c8c9d54b4a139731cd1:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8f9191fe40ae44f5bf190268aa7bb14e"><span data-offset-key="8f9191fe40ae44f5bf190268aa7bb14e:0">Matching Zero or More with the Star</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4dde564a58aa440e8ab549e08fb8f166"><span data-offset-key="4dde564a58aa440e8ab549e08fb8f166:0">The \* (called the star or asterisk) means “match zero or more”—the group that precedes the star can occur any number of times in the text.</span></span></span>

    >>> bat_regex = re.compile(r'Bat(wo)*man')>>> mo1 = bat_regex.search('The Adventures of Batman')>>> mo1.group()'Batman'​>>> mo2 = bat_regex.search('The Adventures of Batwoman')>>> mo2.group()'Batwoman'​>>> mo3 = bat_regex.search('The Adventures of Batwowowowoman')>>> mo3.group()'Batwowowowoman'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="371eaa48ec7c47a0bb88df0fc08e357c"><span data-offset-key="371eaa48ec7c47a0bb88df0fc08e357c:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fb40b450c9954ee4a98de2286a30a375"><span data-offset-key="fb40b450c9954ee4a98de2286a30a375:0">Matching One or More with the Plus</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="acd1c48b02a14ca1a4bd9848c44c79e4"><span data-offset-key="acd1c48b02a14ca1a4bd9848c44c79e4:0">While \* means “match zero or more,” the + (or plus) means “match one or more”. The group preceding a plus must appear at least once. It is not optional:</span></span></span>

    >>> bat_regex = re.compile(r'Bat(wo)+man')>>> mo1 = bat_regex.search('The Adventures of Batwoman')>>> mo1.group()'Batwoman'

    >>> mo2 = bat_regex.search('The Adventures of Batwowowowoman')>>> mo2.group()'Batwowowowoman'

    >>> mo3 = bat_regex.search('The Adventures of Batman')>>> mo3 is NoneTrue

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4f6acf54885148f680aeba2cd79e1432"><span data-offset-key="4f6acf54885148f680aeba2cd79e1432:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bab1378a2956432f9666e5116576ccff"><span data-offset-key="bab1378a2956432f9666e5116576ccff:0">Matching Specific Repetitions with Curly Brackets</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e7809fc039e348bbb7edd535d0a66f55"><span data-offset-key="e7809fc039e348bbb7edd535d0a66f55:0">If you have a group that you want to repeat a specific number of times, follow the group in your regex with a number in curly brackets. For example, the regex (Ha){3} will match the string 'HaHaHa', but it will not match 'HaHa', since the latter has only two repeats of the (Ha) group.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="51a498ed8956497a9f1cc9af342c6e1f"><span data-offset-key="51a498ed8956497a9f1cc9af342c6e1f:0">Instead of one number, you can specify a range by writing a minimum, a comma, and a maximum in between the curly brackets. For example, the regex (Ha){3,5} will match 'HaHaHa', 'HaHaHaHa', and 'HaHaHaHaHa'.</span></span></span>

    >>> ha_regex = re.compile(r'(Ha){3}')>>> mo1 = ha_regex.search('HaHaHa')>>> mo1.group()'HaHaHa'

    >>> mo2 = ha_regex.search('Ha')>>> mo2 is NoneTrue

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9de5716de8284cc4a35f53d3cac472ad"><span data-offset-key="9de5716de8284cc4a35f53d3cac472ad:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5896cba3ac244eba94d43f482a72ff3d"><span data-offset-key="5896cba3ac244eba94d43f482a72ff3d:0">Greedy and Nongreedy Matching</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3bf091f0b8b94d9fa9ef9c4e09dcfa29"><span data-offset-key="3bf091f0b8b94d9fa9ef9c4e09dcfa29:0">Python’s regular expressions are greedy by default, which means that in ambiguous situations they will match the longest string possible. The non-greedy version of the curly brackets, which matches the shortest string possible, has the closing curly bracket followed by a question mark.</span></span></span>

    >>> greedy_ha_regex = re.compile(r'(Ha){3,5}')>>> mo1 = greedy_ha_regex.search('HaHaHaHaHa')>>> mo1.group()'HaHaHaHaHa'

    >>> nongreedy_ha_regex = re.compile(r'(Ha){3,5}?')>>> mo2 = nongreedy_ha_regex.search('HaHaHaHaHa')>>> mo2.group()'HaHaHa'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b9e8fbb300724bd8998db8cc42d0a817"><span data-offset-key="b9e8fbb300724bd8998db8cc42d0a817:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="54aaa932f2354ce082c39ab60d1096a5"><span data-offset-key="54aaa932f2354ce082c39ab60d1096a5:0">The findall() Method</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="bba6308425654353b614fa529fe513c3"><span data-offset-key="bba6308425654353b614fa529fe513c3:0">In addition to the search() method, Regex objects also have a findall() method. While search() will return a Match object of the first matched text in the searched string, the findall() method will return the strings of every match in the searched string.</span></span></span>

    >>> phone_num_regex = re.compile(r'\d\d\d-\d\d\d-\d\d\d\d') # has no groups​>>> phone_num_regex.findall('Cell: 415-555-9999 Work: 212-555-0000')['415-555-9999', '212-555-0000']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="900c5480cb524a86991dd88b2276a338"><span data-offset-key="900c5480cb524a86991dd88b2276a338:0">To summarize what the findall() method returns, remember the following:</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="21c6147a91754dbabf3df38dbba531af"><span data-offset-key="21c6147a91754dbabf3df38dbba531af:0">When called on a regex with no groups, such as \\d-\\d\\d\\d-\\d\\d\\d\\d, the method findall() returns a list of ng matches, such as \['415-555-9999', '212-555-0000'\].</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b887605469ec4eb6aefdb65d87f335fe"><span data-offset-key="b887605469ec4eb6aefdb65d87f335fe:0">When called on a regex that has groups, such as (\\d\\d\\d)-(d\\d)-(\\d\\d\\d\\d), the method findall() returns a list of es of strings (one string for each group), such as \[('415', '555', '9999'), ('212', '555', '0000')\].</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9a7a7f6da9f849c1803a55d44a7ef640"><span data-offset-key="9a7a7f6da9f849c1803a55d44a7ef640:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2b45f452134f4fa994172ea3c7877f6b"><span data-offset-key="2b45f452134f4fa994172ea3c7877f6b:0">Making Your Own Character Classes</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4b38e4a9021445c78eba0b8f49d9bf3f"><span data-offset-key="4b38e4a9021445c78eba0b8f49d9bf3f:0">There are times when you want to match a set of characters but the shorthand character classes (\\d, \\w, \\s, and so on) are too broad. You can define your own character class using square brackets. For example, the character class \[aeiouAEIOU\] will match any vowel, both lowercase and uppercase.</span></span></span>

    >>> vowel_regex = re.compile(r'[aeiouAEIOU]')​>>> vowel_regex.findall('Robocop eats baby food. BABY FOOD.')['o', 'o', 'o', 'e', 'a', 'a', 'o', 'o', 'A', 'O', 'O']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="644ee3dba0144a0baf75ae04a40607ea"><span data-offset-key="644ee3dba0144a0baf75ae04a40607ea:0">You can also include ranges of letters or numbers by using a hyphen. For example, the character class \[a-zA-Z0-9\] will match all lowercase letters, uppercase letters, and numbers.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fa3f83ef5d9b43b490efe9377ecbbfb3"><span data-offset-key="fa3f83ef5d9b43b490efe9377ecbbfb3:0">By placing a caret character (^) just after the character class’s opening bracket, you can make a negative character class. A negative character class will match all the characters that are not in the character class. For example, enter the following into the interactive shell:</span></span></span>

    >>> consonant_regex = re.compile(r'[^aeiouAEIOU]')​>>> consonant_regex.findall('Robocop eats baby food. BABY FOOD.')['R', 'b', 'c', 'p', ' ', 't', 's', ' ', 'b', 'b', 'y', ' ', 'f', 'd', '.', '', 'B', 'B', 'Y', ' ', 'F', 'D', '.']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c8925d1bdfe44800b10fb2e885e6a685"><span data-offset-key="c8925d1bdfe44800b10fb2e885e6a685:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="408365d3b318445d8974598a8c73a271"><span data-offset-key="408365d3b318445d8974598a8c73a271:0">The Caret and Dollar Sign Characters</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d397a9186d35423386dd18adfc20d38f"><span data-offset-key="d397a9186d35423386dd18adfc20d38f:0">You can also use the caret symbol (^) at the start of a regex to indicate that a match must occur at the beginning of the searched text.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9a9972cc3baa4d12b8f1efc022bc8b0f"><span data-offset-key="9a9972cc3baa4d12b8f1efc022bc8b0f:0">Likewise, you can put a dollar sign ($) at the end of the regex to indicate the string must end with this regex pattern.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="68b8eb5a5dc648d1a1ae3c463617afae"><span data-offset-key="68b8eb5a5dc648d1a1ae3c463617afae:0">And you can use the ^ and $ together to indicate that the entire string must match the regex—that is, it’s not enough for a match to be made on some subset of the string.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b08d511c203043a4b6ba4c8650209d46"><span data-offset-key="b08d511c203043a4b6ba4c8650209d46:0">The r'^Hello' regular expression string matches strings that begin with 'Hello':</span></span></span>

    >>> begins_with_hello = re.compile(r'^Hello')​>>> begins_with_hello.search('Hello world!')<_sre.SRE_Match object; span=(0, 5), match='Hello'>​>>> begins_with_hello.search('He said hello.') is NoneTrue

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6416469b11e6455a958ef273c6b54de4"><span data-offset-key="6416469b11e6455a958ef273c6b54de4:0">The r'\\d$' regular expression string matches strings that end with a numeric character from 0 to 9:</span></span></span>

    >>> whole_string_is_num = re.compile(r'^\d+$')​>>> whole_string_is_num.search('1234567890')<_sre.SRE_Match object; span=(0, 10), match='1234567890'>​>>> whole_string_is_num.search('12345xyz67890') is NoneTrue​>>> whole_string_is_num.search('12 34567890') is NoneTrue

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="46d8797f65f641f285835e1d7716c26c"><span data-offset-key="46d8797f65f641f285835e1d7716c26c:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1c0280e012f5402587487ec935580700"><span data-offset-key="1c0280e012f5402587487ec935580700:0">The Wildcard Character</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6449ff1f016748058bb7b37153a22bcd"><span data-offset-key="6449ff1f016748058bb7b37153a22bcd:0">The . (or dot) character in a regular expression is called a wildcard and will match any character except for a newline:</span></span></span>

    >>> at_regex = re.compile(r'.at')​>>> at_regex.findall('The cat in the hat sat on the flat mat.')['cat', 'hat', 'sat', 'lat', 'mat']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="66de9430e46c4dbb852b6337b589f6be"><span data-offset-key="66de9430e46c4dbb852b6337b589f6be:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9958e028d913433ba0e7d53466b6c2c7"><span data-offset-key="9958e028d913433ba0e7d53466b6c2c7:0">Matching Everything with Dot-Star</span></span></span>

    >>> name_regex = re.compile(r'First Name: (.*) Last Name: (.*)')​>>> mo = name_regex.search('First Name: Al Last Name: Sweigart')​>>> mo.group(1)'Al'

    >>> mo.group(2)'Sweigart'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9eb7ab44e233448496a5b9195c316d52"><span data-offset-key="9eb7ab44e233448496a5b9195c316d52:0">The dot-star uses greedy mode: It will always try to match as much text as possible. To match any and all text in a nongreedy fashion, use the dot, star, and question mark (.\*?). The question mark tells Python to match in a nongreedy way:</span></span></span>

    >>> nongreedy_regex = re.compile(r'<.*?>')>>> mo = nongreedy_regex.search('<To serve man> for dinner.>')>>> mo.group()'<To serve man>'

    >>> greedy_regex = re.compile(r'<.*>')>>> mo = greedy_regex.search('<To serve man> for dinner.>')>>> mo.group()'<To serve man> for dinner.>'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0ebeede4fdf34816861d224c7eac7781"><span data-offset-key="0ebeede4fdf34816861d224c7eac7781:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9ca63b6b1b884c5b852248326a79a5cd"><span data-offset-key="9ca63b6b1b884c5b852248326a79a5cd:0">Matching Newlines with the Dot Character</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="266ef2c84e0a4492b89dc8aef64d9dba"><span data-offset-key="266ef2c84e0a4492b89dc8aef64d9dba:0">The dot-star will match everything except a newline. By passing re.DOTALL as the second argument to re.compile(), you can make the dot character match all characters, including the newline character:</span></span></span>

    >>> no_newline_regex = re.compile('.*')>>> no_newline_regex.search('Serve the public trust.\nProtect the innocent.\nUphold the law.').group()'Serve the public trust.'

    >>> newline_regex = re.compile('.*', re.DOTALL)>>> newline_regex.search('Serve the public trust.\nProtect the innocent.\nUphold the law.').group()'Serve the public trust.\nProtect the innocent.\nUphold the law.'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a9e6db7b6de74bb8970783cb7cab8ce2"><span data-offset-key="a9e6db7b6de74bb8970783cb7cab8ce2:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2c50ee629ac9420a8914fa87aae30bfe"><span data-offset-key="2c50ee629ac9420a8914fa87aae30bfe:0">Review of Regex Symbols</span></span></span>

preceding group.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="odd"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span more of the preceding group.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="odd"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ed0e87d6bde44be698c3816d90dd9ed9"><span data-offset-key="ed0e87d6bde44be698c3816d90dd9ed9:0">0 to m of the preceding group.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="even"><td left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a987b589a4434065a04d0f01a69da015"><span data-offset-key="a987b589a4434065a04d0f01a69da015:0">at least n and at most m of the preceding p.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="odd"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="10d2d324a5dd4ef3bd0089f6f4cfa7b8"><span data-offset-key="10d2d324a5dd4ef3bd0089f6f4cfa7b8:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">{n,m}?</code></span><span data-offset-key="10d2d324a5dd4ef3bd0089f6f4cfa7b8:1"> or </span><span or </span><span data-offset-key="10d2d324a5dd4ef3bd0089f6f4cfa7b8:4"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">+?</code></span></span></span></p></td><td style="text-align: data-offset-key="c0e3730f33fb41fcb9d36d740456ebb3:0">performs a nongreedy match of the preceding p.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="even"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span begin with spam.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="odd"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8816e0b0e2e345b69873f1e76f566e8e"><span data-offset-key="8816e0b0e2e345b69873f1e76f566e8e:0">any character, except newline characters.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="odd"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-offset-key="44c57f7ff4824e82bdf4a08d7170b641:1">, </span><span data-offset-key="44c57f7ff4824e82bdf4a08d7170b641:2"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">\s</code></span></span></span></p></td><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8c6ad8267b2047a0914ae58f4f50efe9"><span data-offset-key="8c6ad8267b2047a0914ae58f4f50efe9:0">a digit, word, or space character, respectively.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="even"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6e81f5ef07d74a599ea5e3116b86ba23"><span data-offset-key="6e81f5ef07d74a599ea5e3116b86ba23:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">\D</code></span><span data-offset-key="6e81f5ef07d74a599ea5e3116b86ba23:1">, </span><span data-offset-key="6e81f5ef07d74a599ea5e3116b86ba23:2"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">\W</code></span><span data-key="9c8cec3154294f899698f7c0ec15ea7f"><span data-offset-key="9c8cec3154294f899698f7c0ec15ea7f:0">anything except a digit, word, or space, respectively.</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="odd"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2214a95abc484d7c849bcda592341b47"><span data-offset-key="2214a95abc484d7c849bcda592341b47:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">[abc]</code></span></span></span></p></td><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a0e4632579c544eeb5fdc80603ba9859"><span data-offset-key="a0e4632579c544eeb5fdc80603ba9859:0">any character between the brackets (such as a, b, ).</span></span></span></p></td></tr><tr class="even"><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="82bd4513d3ef477abbb5a006c13aac56"><span data-offset-key="82bd4513d3ef477abbb5a006c13aac56:0"><code class="code-0458e21e" spellcheck="false" data-slate-leaf="true">[^abc]</code></span></span></span></p></td><td style="text-align: left;"><p><span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0c46c2b78ef74fca8200cbee04549f62"><span data-offset-key="0c46c2b78ef74fca8200cbee04549f62:0">any character that isn’t between the brackets.</span></span></span></p></td></tr></tbody></table>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="20d52d08a8604d0db1761a06a1fe527d"><span data-offset-key="20d52d08a8604d0db1761a06a1fe527d:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5bdc984c9e794056a19ace2fa9da2fed"><span data-offset-key="5bdc984c9e794056a19ace2fa9da2fed:0">Case-Insensitive Matching</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d1019f435b864863a2592387cd1fd0bf"><span data-offset-key="d1019f435b864863a2592387cd1fd0bf:0">To make your regex case-insensitive, you can pass re.IGNORECASE or re.I as a second argument to re.compile():</span></span></span>

    >>> robocop = re.compile(r'robocop', re.I)​>>> robocop.search('Robocop is part man, part machine, all cop.').group()'Robocop'

    >>> robocop.search('ROBOCOP protects the innocent.').group()'ROBOCOP'

    >>> robocop.search('Al, why does your programming book talk about robocop so much?').group()'robocop'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5eea25b1ed944037a9e8306b97357b1c"><span data-offset-key="5eea25b1ed944037a9e8306b97357b1c:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="eb6b8f976bfb43b39d00da98cf0aa5a4"><span data-offset-key="eb6b8f976bfb43b39d00da98cf0aa5a4:0">Substituting Strings with the sub() Method</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b96828d6afdf43ffa8953effac23abdf"><span data-offset-key="b96828d6afdf43ffa8953effac23abdf:0">The sub() method for Regex objects is passed two arguments:</span></span></span>

1.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="afeb94a27b414e809cad62ddf72e8714"><span data-offset-key="afeb94a27b414e809cad62ddf72e8714:0">The first argument is a string to replace any matches.</span></span></span>

2.  <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="34ea9ae8f0604a8785940885b93f8f44"><span data-offset-key="34ea9ae8f0604a8785940885b93f8f44:0">The second is the string for the regular expression.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3e94766a716f4f6f8003e48bd0267789"><span data-offset-key="3e94766a716f4f6f8003e48bd0267789:0">The sub() method returns a string with the substitutions applied:</span></span></span>

    >>> names_regex = re.compile(r'Agent \w+')​>>> names_regex.sub('CENSORED', 'Agent Alice gave the secret documents to Agent Bob.')'CENSORED gave the secret documents to CENSORED.'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b4b83e0a65484252a0814b8576c5c74e"><span data-offset-key="b4b83e0a65484252a0814b8576c5c74e:0">Another example:</span></span></span>

    >>> agent_names_regex = re.compile(r'Agent (\w)\w*')​>>> agent_names_regex.sub(r'\1****', 'Agent Alice told Agent Carol that Agent Eve knew Agent Bob was a double agent.')A**** told C**** that E**** knew B**** was a double agent.'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="839df2df43814245961abaabb1390e13"><span data-offset-key="839df2df43814245961abaabb1390e13:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="95292a77d35448f789c6b4ba97602372"><span data-offset-key="95292a77d35448f789c6b4ba97602372:0">Managing Complex Regexes</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="db648e3c3ee34ff9b65537fe61d4707b"><span data-offset-key="db648e3c3ee34ff9b65537fe61d4707b:0">To tell the re.compile() function to ignore whitespace and comments inside the regular expression string, “verbose mode” can be enabled by passing the variable re.VERBOSE as the second argument to re.compile().</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c07f32dc78574fa2a06d092896ccbe1d"><span data-offset-key="c07f32dc78574fa2a06d092896ccbe1d:0">Now instead of a hard-to-read regular expression like this:</span></span></span>

    phone_regex = re.compile(r'((\d{3}|\(\d{3}\))?(\s|-|\.)?\d{3}(\s|-|\.)\d{4}(\s*(ext|x|ext.)\s*\d{2,5})?)')

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b3350b317724424d8626e4137a3bee82"><span data-offset-key="b3350b317724424d8626e4137a3bee82:0">you can spread the regular expression over multiple lines with comments like this:</span></span></span>

    phone_regex = re.compile(r'''(    (\d{3}|\(\d{3}\))?            # area code    (\s|-|\.)?                    # separator    \d{3}                         # first 3 digits    (\s|-|\.)                     # separator    \d{4}                         # last 4 digits    (\s*(ext|x|ext.)\s*\d{2,5})?  # extension    )''', re.VERBOSE)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="16ad5d5e1a1c4158b2886f16f8988d88"><span data-offset-key="16ad5d5e1a1c4158b2886f16f8988d88:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a29d89bf2856400f90b419b8db673b38"><span data-offset-key="a29d89bf2856400f90b419b8db673b38:0">Handling File and Directory Paths</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="79e30d63bdd24ad19f48ad0c1f317888"><span data-offset-key="79e30d63bdd24ad19f48ad0c1f317888:0">There are two main modules in Python that deals with path manipulation. One is the </span><span data-offset-key="79e30d63bdd24ad19f48ad0c1f317888:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="79e30d63bdd24ad19f48ad0c1f317888:2"> module and the other is the </span><span data-offset-key="79e30d63bdd24ad19f48ad0c1f317888:3">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="79e30d63bdd24ad19f48ad0c1f317888:4"> module. The </span><span data-offset-key="79e30d63bdd24ad19f48ad0c1f317888:5">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="79e30d63bdd24ad19f48ad0c1f317888:6"> module was added in Python 3.4, offering an object-oriented way to handle file system paths.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8c82d0c1c3d44272a51533152e067ffb"><span data-offset-key="8c82d0c1c3d44272a51533152e067ffb:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="11c687e9d6c24eadbd58d5ffd8b1e3bf"><span data-offset-key="11c687e9d6c24eadbd58d5ffd8b1e3bf:0">Backslash on Windows and Forward Slash on OS X and Linux</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5a131d188ef64c368b4041a9f22cb546"><span data-offset-key="5a131d188ef64c368b4041a9f22cb546:0">On Windows, paths are written using backslashes (</span><span data-offset-key="5a131d188ef64c368b4041a9f22cb546:1">`\`</span><span data-offset-key="5a131d188ef64c368b4041a9f22cb546:2">) as the separator between folder names. On Unix based operating system such as macOS, Linux, and BSDs, the forward slash (</span><span data-offset-key="5a131d188ef64c368b4041a9f22cb546:3">`/`</span><span data-offset-key="5a131d188ef64c368b4041a9f22cb546:4">) is used as the path separator. Joining paths can be a headache if your code needs to work on different platforms.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a570b7b77456420b8ae9bfda07b82e88"><span data-offset-key="a570b7b77456420b8ae9bfda07b82e88:0">Fortunately, Python provides easy ways to handle this. We will showcase how to deal with this with both </span><span data-offset-key="a570b7b77456420b8ae9bfda07b82e88:1">`os.path.join`</span><span data-offset-key="a570b7b77456420b8ae9bfda07b82e88:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="a570b7b77456420b8ae9bfda07b82e88:3">`pathlib.Path.joinpath`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e5b8c73508654134b3edd83a92fe7ade"><span data-offset-key="e5b8c73508654134b3edd83a92fe7ade:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="e5b8c73508654134b3edd83a92fe7ade:1">`os.path.join`</span><span data-offset-key="e5b8c73508654134b3edd83a92fe7ade:2"> on Windows:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os​>>> os.path.join('usr', 'bin', 'spam')'usr\\bin\\spam'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ddb95ab4c21345ff928f704c29c28241"><span data-offset-key="ddb95ab4c21345ff928f704c29c28241:0">And using </span><span data-offset-key="ddb95ab4c21345ff928f704c29c28241:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="ddb95ab4c21345ff928f704c29c28241:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path​>>> print(Path('usr').joinpath('bin').joinpath('spam'))usr/bin/spam

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="967707f35240424585f58527a0e8b3a6"><span data-offset-key="967707f35240424585f58527a0e8b3a6:0">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="967707f35240424585f58527a0e8b3a6:1"> also provides a shortcut to joinpath using the </span><span data-offset-key="967707f35240424585f58527a0e8b3a6:2">`/`</span><span data-offset-key="967707f35240424585f58527a0e8b3a6:3"> operator:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path​>>> print(Path('usr') / 'bin' / 'spam')usr/bin/spam

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0c4a1234ee074bad91eb13ba3a44adf8"><span data-offset-key="0c4a1234ee074bad91eb13ba3a44adf8:0">Notice the path separator is different between Windows and Unix based operating system, that's why you want to use one of the above methods instead of adding strings together to join paths together.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ea4338b368e04b4db3d86baed27e95df"><span data-offset-key="ea4338b368e04b4db3d86baed27e95df:0">Joining paths is helpful if you need to create different file paths under the same directory.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="479e13e5cd5043b582f8bcfce550e1cc"><span data-offset-key="479e13e5cd5043b582f8bcfce550e1cc:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="479e13e5cd5043b582f8bcfce550e1cc:1">`os.path.join`</span><span data-offset-key="479e13e5cd5043b582f8bcfce550e1cc:2"> on Windows:</span></span></span>

    >>> my_files = ['accounts.txt', 'details.csv', 'invite.docx']​>>> for filename in my_files:>>>     print(os.path.join('C:\\Users\\asweigart', filename))C:\Users\asweigart\accounts.txtC:\Users\asweigart\details.csvC:\Users\asweigart\invite.docx

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c548a63ea61e4daab5c3113965014c9d"><span data-offset-key="c548a63ea61e4daab5c3113965014c9d:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="c548a63ea61e4daab5c3113965014c9d:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="c548a63ea61e4daab5c3113965014c9d:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> my_files = ['accounts.txt', 'details.csv', 'invite.docx']>>> home = Path.home()>>> for filename in my_files:>>>     print(home / filename)/home/asweigart/accounts.txt/home/asweigart/details.csv/home/asweigart/invite.docx

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="28b685cb056541a6bdeacce460053cdd"><span data-offset-key="28b685cb056541a6bdeacce460053cdd:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="207b3738c7dd40a8b335e38c01a79058"><span data-offset-key="207b3738c7dd40a8b335e38c01a79058:0">The Current Working Directory</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f1c47fdc76f04379a2f6b3eb2cf96af4"><span data-offset-key="f1c47fdc76f04379a2f6b3eb2cf96af4:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="f1c47fdc76f04379a2f6b3eb2cf96af4:1">`os`</span><span data-offset-key="f1c47fdc76f04379a2f6b3eb2cf96af4:2"> on Windows:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os​>>> os.getcwd()'C:\\Python34'>>> os.chdir('C:\\Windows\\System32')​>>> os.getcwd()'C:\\Windows\\System32'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="de4c48f76de4453fb27b0a12114e0f16"><span data-offset-key="de4c48f76de4453fb27b0a12114e0f16:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="de4c48f76de4453fb27b0a12114e0f16:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="de4c48f76de4453fb27b0a12114e0f16:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> from os import chdir​>>> print(Path.cwd())/home/asweigart​>>> chdir('/usr/lib/python3.6')>>> print(Path.cwd())/usr/lib/python3.6

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="1ce8237e2396408b89d7c1214704aade"><span data-offset-key="1ce8237e2396408b89d7c1214704aade:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fd86a176e760499fb71b6ba6dd61eede"><span data-offset-key="fd86a176e760499fb71b6ba6dd61eede:0">Creating New Folders</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b0f151a68ef4448cb916855025ddf64e"><span data-offset-key="b0f151a68ef4448cb916855025ddf64e:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="b0f151a68ef4448cb916855025ddf64e:1">`os`</span><span data-offset-key="b0f151a68ef4448cb916855025ddf64e:2"> on Windows:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> os.makedirs('C:\\delicious\\walnut\\waffles')

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3abfb257431e453e9fc6d119b98125bd"><span data-offset-key="3abfb257431e453e9fc6d119b98125bd:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="3abfb257431e453e9fc6d119b98125bd:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="3abfb257431e453e9fc6d119b98125bd:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> cwd = Path.cwd()>>> (cwd / 'delicious' / 'walnut' / 'waffles').mkdir()Traceback (most recent call last):  File "<stdin>", line 1, in <module>  File "/usr/lib/python3.6/pathlib.py", line 1226, in mkdir    self._accessor.mkdir(self, mode)  File "/usr/lib/python3.6/pathlib.py", line 387, in wrapped    return strfunc(str(pathobj), *args)FileNotFoundError: [Errno 2] No such file or directory: '/home/asweigart/delicious/walnut/waffles'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5a26799ad8fd4b2da8694564a484fdaa"><span data-offset-key="5a26799ad8fd4b2da8694564a484fdaa:0">Oh no, we got a nasty error! The reason is that the 'delicious' directory does not exist, so we cannot make the 'walnut' and the 'waffles' directories under it. To fix this, do:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> cwd = Path.cwd()>>> (cwd / 'delicious' / 'walnut' / 'waffles').mkdir(parents=True)

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="91d80bb366f84d58b31e2089a4e35182"><span data-offset-key="91d80bb366f84d58b31e2089a4e35182:0">And all is good :)</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="475d2c49c41d47c9b0f00653d33ada97"><span data-offset-key="475d2c49c41d47c9b0f00653d33ada97:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0bdeee003e5642128cac2ae34c0b1878"><span data-offset-key="0bdeee003e5642128cac2ae34c0b1878:0">Absolute vs. Relative Paths</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d66416ffb10c4aed99c89e96ee1d0032"><span data-offset-key="d66416ffb10c4aed99c89e96ee1d0032:0">There are two ways to specify a file path.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="88318b88af54429296207c2fda81a7ea"><span data-offset-key="88318b88af54429296207c2fda81a7ea:0">An absolute path, which always begins with the root folder</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="00aebd7350e34391a8b125fff873484f"><span data-offset-key="00aebd7350e34391a8b125fff873484f:0">A relative path, which is relative to the program’s current working directory</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4b0c1fc92087441e89f9cefe4cb9136c"><span data-offset-key="4b0c1fc92087441e89f9cefe4cb9136c:0">There are also the dot (.) and dot-dot (..) folders. These are not real folders but special names that can be used in a path. A single period (“dot”) for a folder name is shorthand for “this directory.” Two periods (“dot-dot”) means “the parent folder.”</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a6944d69a6b34f92adda678b6ac47b67"><span data-offset-key="a6944d69a6b34f92adda678b6ac47b67:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="5feed11dc84040c7a883704f531b2f59"><span data-offset-key="5feed11dc84040c7a883704f531b2f59:0">Handling Absolute and Relative Paths</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d802e612373b426e9fd47d7acca87b47"><span data-offset-key="d802e612373b426e9fd47d7acca87b47:0">To see if a path is an absolute path:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e83041271a464fdb9b21753bcfccda66"><span data-offset-key="e83041271a464fdb9b21753bcfccda66:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="e83041271a464fdb9b21753bcfccda66:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="e83041271a464fdb9b21753bcfccda66:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> os.path.isabs('/')True>>> os.path.isabs('..')False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0f5ada637a68408e8e306bc042fdd8bb"><span data-offset-key="0f5ada637a68408e8e306bc042fdd8bb:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="0f5ada637a68408e8e306bc042fdd8bb:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="0f5ada637a68408e8e306bc042fdd8bb:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> Path('/').is_absolute()True>>> Path('..').is_absolute()False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a6b2d20a6259417e861445e2ad47fb8d"><span data-offset-key="a6b2d20a6259417e861445e2ad47fb8d:0">You can extract an absolute path with both </span><span data-offset-key="a6b2d20a6259417e861445e2ad47fb8d:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="a6b2d20a6259417e861445e2ad47fb8d:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="a6b2d20a6259417e861445e2ad47fb8d:3">`pathlib`</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7f644e65d2114a999d7812562cd3ac8a"><span data-offset-key="7f644e65d2114a999d7812562cd3ac8a:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="7f644e65d2114a999d7812562cd3ac8a:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="7f644e65d2114a999d7812562cd3ac8a:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> os.getcwd()'/home/asweigart'>>> os.path.abspath('..')'/home'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="efdbd45c69c54ed0a70dc0c24c5f718b"><span data-offset-key="efdbd45c69c54ed0a70dc0c24c5f718b:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="efdbd45c69c54ed0a70dc0c24c5f718b:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="efdbd45c69c54ed0a70dc0c24c5f718b:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    from pathlib import Pathprint(Path.cwd())/home/asweigartprint(Path('..').resolve())/home

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="efd2a64d68a84acbac3c20849218d4c5"><span data-offset-key="efd2a64d68a84acbac3c20849218d4c5:0">You can get a relative path from a starting path to another path.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="170d3eb0d610418ba830f3ab0d7eb22d"><span data-offset-key="170d3eb0d610418ba830f3ab0d7eb22d:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="170d3eb0d610418ba830f3ab0d7eb22d:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="170d3eb0d610418ba830f3ab0d7eb22d:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> os.path.relpath('/etc/passwd', '/')'etc/passwd'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4a258f2e77b847e2859c6210e7817023"><span data-offset-key="4a258f2e77b847e2859c6210e7817023:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="4a258f2e77b847e2859c6210e7817023:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="4a258f2e77b847e2859c6210e7817023:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> print(Path('/etc/passwd').relative_to('/'))etc/passwd

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="79bf0b54d045409ea62a4a52a1d24179"><span data-offset-key="79bf0b54d045409ea62a4a52a1d24179:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3ae1493988a14537a746e0fdba77ac91"><span data-offset-key="3ae1493988a14537a746e0fdba77ac91:0">Checking Path Validity</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="357a83b4a8384cc5ab28c9c5695d1692"><span data-offset-key="357a83b4a8384cc5ab28c9c5695d1692:0">Checking if a file/directory exists:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="630fd379ce6846c0bc5c43b52a18fee3"><span data-offset-key="630fd379ce6846c0bc5c43b52a18fee3:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="630fd379ce6846c0bc5c43b52a18fee3:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="630fd379ce6846c0bc5c43b52a18fee3:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    import os>>> os.path.exists('.')True>>> os.path.exists('setup.py')True>>> os.path.exists('/etc')True>>> os.path.exists('nonexistentfile')False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3ee81c0f34e84f0db19b70787cf36951"><span data-offset-key="3ee81c0f34e84f0db19b70787cf36951:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="3ee81c0f34e84f0db19b70787cf36951:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="3ee81c0f34e84f0db19b70787cf36951:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    from pathlib import Path>>> Path('.').exists()True>>> Path('setup.py').exists()True>>> Path('/etc').exists()True>>> Path('nonexistentfile').exists()False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a3749a744a4a45a2ac70b9e14332b3e9"><span data-offset-key="a3749a744a4a45a2ac70b9e14332b3e9:0">Checking if a path is a file:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="98d66c9925cd4b778ae2f8bf32ada56c"><span data-offset-key="98d66c9925cd4b778ae2f8bf32ada56c:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="98d66c9925cd4b778ae2f8bf32ada56c:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="98d66c9925cd4b778ae2f8bf32ada56c:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> os.path.isfile('setup.py')True>>> os.path.isfile('/home')False>>> os.path.isfile('nonexistentfile')False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3881f5b556544284b7cbc7befa079b00"><span data-offset-key="3881f5b556544284b7cbc7befa079b00:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="3881f5b556544284b7cbc7befa079b00:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="3881f5b556544284b7cbc7befa079b00:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> Path('setup.py').is_file()True>>> Path('/home').is_file()False>>> Path('nonexistentfile').is_file()False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0ebaf68381894fd2b7cd98077e0c5343"><span data-offset-key="0ebaf68381894fd2b7cd98077e0c5343:0">Checking if a path is a directory:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="67c6045b1e384d8092d866da81a46a43"><span data-offset-key="67c6045b1e384d8092d866da81a46a43:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="67c6045b1e384d8092d866da81a46a43:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="67c6045b1e384d8092d866da81a46a43:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> os.path.isdir('/')True>>> os.path.isdir('setup.py')False>>> os.path.isdir('/spam')False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f07abf315b4643498c931a1a617dc354"><span data-offset-key="f07abf315b4643498c931a1a617dc354:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="f07abf315b4643498c931a1a617dc354:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="f07abf315b4643498c931a1a617dc354:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> Path('/').is_dir()True>>> Path('setup.py').is_dir()False>>> Path('/spam').is_dir()False

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6b962e2e789b4e67a61c10f6243c7561"><span data-offset-key="6b962e2e789b4e67a61c10f6243c7561:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a8090f1666154dd49838238b92c8ba01"><span data-offset-key="a8090f1666154dd49838238b92c8ba01:0">Finding File Sizes and Folder Contents</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="44e59d79c4454faead14de76db0c290e"><span data-offset-key="44e59d79c4454faead14de76db0c290e:0">Getting a file's size in bytes:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="e03a527bb6074e9e91998f546cf7bc67"><span data-offset-key="e03a527bb6074e9e91998f546cf7bc67:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="e03a527bb6074e9e91998f546cf7bc67:1">`os.path`</span><span data-offset-key="e03a527bb6074e9e91998f546cf7bc67:2"> on Windows:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> os.path.getsize('C:\\Windows\\System32\\calc.exe')776192

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7c5807e010154e7885cf968054add8de"><span data-offset-key="7c5807e010154e7885cf968054add8de:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="7c5807e010154e7885cf968054add8de:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="7c5807e010154e7885cf968054add8de:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> stat = Path('/bin/python3.6').stat()>>> print(stat) # stat contains some other information about the file as wellos.stat_result(st_mode=33261, st_ino=141087, st_dev=2051, st_nlink=2, st_uid=0,--snip--st_gid=0, st_size=10024, st_atime=1517725562, st_mtime=1515119809, st_ctime=1517261276)>>> print(stat.st_size) # size in bytes10024

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="2362a032c9084728a383922dc817435d"><span data-offset-key="2362a032c9084728a383922dc817435d:0">Listing directory contents using </span><span data-offset-key="2362a032c9084728a383922dc817435d:1">`os.listdir`</span><span data-offset-key="2362a032c9084728a383922dc817435d:2"> on Windows:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> os.listdir('C:\\Windows\\System32')['0409', '12520437.cpx', '12520850.cpx', '5U877.ax', 'aaclient.dll',--snip--'xwtpdui.dll', 'xwtpw32.dll', 'zh-CN', 'zh-HK', 'zh-TW', 'zipfldr.dll']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4f5846b0fee149d1afed27548d29f011"><span data-offset-key="4f5846b0fee149d1afed27548d29f011:0">Listing directory contents using </span><span data-offset-key="4f5846b0fee149d1afed27548d29f011:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="4f5846b0fee149d1afed27548d29f011:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> for f in Path('/usr/bin').iterdir():>>>     print(f).../usr/bin/tiff2rgba/usr/bin/iconv/usr/bin/ldd/usr/bin/cache_restore/usr/bin/udiskie/usr/bin/unix2dos/usr/bin/t1reencode/usr/bin/epstopdf/usr/bin/idle3...

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="fe98c7cbede84beaa6ee6d66cc76e40f"><span data-offset-key="fe98c7cbede84beaa6ee6d66cc76e40f:0">To find the total size of all the files in this directory:</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0e41a82bdf224dd39cb73cf34aaf30ea"><span data-offset-key="0e41a82bdf224dd39cb73cf34aaf30ea:0">**WARNING**</span><span data-offset-key="0e41a82bdf224dd39cb73cf34aaf30ea:1">: Directories themselves also have a size! So you might want to check for whether a path is a file or directory using the methods in the methods discussed in the above section!</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="939872ef9dcc4cf1b0b94e44e4437b08"><span data-offset-key="939872ef9dcc4cf1b0b94e44e4437b08:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="939872ef9dcc4cf1b0b94e44e4437b08:1">`os.path.getsize()`</span><span data-offset-key="939872ef9dcc4cf1b0b94e44e4437b08:2"> and </span><span data-offset-key="939872ef9dcc4cf1b0b94e44e4437b08:3">`os.listdir()`</span><span data-offset-key="939872ef9dcc4cf1b0b94e44e4437b08:4"> together on Windows:</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>> total_size = 0​>>> for filename in os.listdir('C:\\Windows\\System32'):      total_size = total_size + os.path.getsize(os.path.join('C:\\Windows\\System32', filename))​>>> print(total_size)1117846456

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0db49a6805e74d059524fa749041a91a"><span data-offset-key="0db49a6805e74d059524fa749041a91a:0">Using </span><span data-offset-key="0db49a6805e74d059524fa749041a91a:1">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="0db49a6805e74d059524fa749041a91a:2"> on \*nix:</span></span></span>

    >>> from pathlib import Path>>> total_size = 0​>>> for sub_path in Path('/usr/bin').iterdir():...     total_size += sub_path.stat().st_size>>>>>> print(total_size)1903178911

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="76c2d7ea44e24d7fb15d02da5cf828b8"><span data-offset-key="76c2d7ea44e24d7fb15d02da5cf828b8:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7a9c4eb00c0245ce96112fdffa7584c8"><span data-offset-key="7a9c4eb00c0245ce96112fdffa7584c8:0">Copying Files and Folders</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="92e58bcc74d34c6ba42ff7cd39e1626d"><span data-offset-key="92e58bcc74d34c6ba42ff7cd39e1626d:0">The shutil module provides functions for copying files, as well as entire folders.</span></span></span>

    >>> import shutil, os​>>> os.chdir('C:\\')​>>> shutil.copy('C:\\spam.txt', 'C:\\delicious')   'C:\\delicious\\spam.txt'​>>> shutil.copy('eggs.txt', 'C:\\delicious\\eggs2.txt')   'C:\\delicious\\eggs2.txt'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="578a0e9f9ce9475e88e85286481d717a"><span data-offset-key="578a0e9f9ce9475e88e85286481d717a:0">While shutil.copy() will copy a single file, shutil.copytree() will copy an entire folder and every folder and file contained in it:</span></span></span>

    >>> import shutil, os​>>> os.chdir('C:\\')​>>> shutil.copytree('C:\\bacon', 'C:\\bacon_backup')'C:\\bacon_backup'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="da26f4b84e944946bb948324784abbe2"><span data-offset-key="da26f4b84e944946bb948324784abbe2:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="43179906b8b04e5cad691ae76f9fb9fb"><span data-offset-key="43179906b8b04e5cad691ae76f9fb9fb:0">Moving and Renaming Files and Folders</span></span></span>

    >>> import shutil>>> shutil.move('C:\\bacon.txt', 'C:\\eggs')'C:\\eggs\\bacon.txt'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ca918637b5004c52bcbe15b9fa751c04"><span data-offset-key="ca918637b5004c52bcbe15b9fa751c04:0">The destination path can also specify a filename. In the following example, the source file is moved and renamed:</span></span></span>

    >>> shutil.move('C:\\bacon.txt', 'C:\\eggs\\new_bacon.txt')'C:\\eggs\\new_bacon.txt'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="413d1b1e2da74882a78e4cd04a26403e"><span data-offset-key="413d1b1e2da74882a78e4cd04a26403e:0">If there is no eggs folder, then move() will rename bacon.txt to a file named eggs.</span></span></span>

    >>> shutil.move('C:\\bacon.txt', 'C:\\eggs')'C:\\eggs'

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ab227ee40bcd4cb48b274996dcb6adac"><span data-offset-key="ab227ee40bcd4cb48b274996dcb6adac:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="53e71673886845f7a8b8523f58ca314f"><span data-offset-key="53e71673886845f7a8b8523f58ca314f:0">Permanently Deleting Files and Folders</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="7db4e0c23feb4425b6c35b39f7ae8a32"><span data-offset-key="7db4e0c23feb4425b6c35b39f7ae8a32:0">Calling os.unlink(path) or Path.unlink() will delete the file at path.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="cf805cde327c413d9053cffbcbee330f"><span data-offset-key="cf805cde327c413d9053cffbcbee330f:0">Calling os.rmdir(path) or Path.rmdir() will delete the folder at path. This folder must be empty of any files or folders.</span></span></span>

-   <span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c955ffe9a349437d9af41c95256e6156"><span data-offset-key="c955ffe9a349437d9af41c95256e6156:0">Calling shutil.rmtree(path) will remove the folder at path, and all files and folders it contains will also be deleted.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="a1a780851aa54c63a157d25544dfe754"><span data-offset-key="a1a780851aa54c63a157d25544dfe754:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="4409917edcff429a852999e97ac7d3b3"><span data-offset-key="4409917edcff429a852999e97ac7d3b3:0">Safe Deletes with the send2trash Module</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="b75f758d71984faaaeacbf1b8189535a"><span data-offset-key="b75f758d71984faaaeacbf1b8189535a:0">You can install this module by running pip install send2trash from a Terminal window.</span></span></span>

    >>> import send2trash​>>> with open('bacon.txt', 'a') as bacon_file: # creates the file...     bacon_file.write('Bacon is not a vegetable.')25​>>> send2trash.send2trash('bacon.txt')

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="eb8cfe47667c46b3ac0074fcafcf512f"><span data-offset-key="eb8cfe47667c46b3ac0074fcafcf512f:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="6fde7db243b44760b92b35cdcd761fb3"><span data-offset-key="6fde7db243b44760b92b35cdcd761fb3:0">Walking a Directory Tree</span></span></span>

    >>> import os>>>>>> for folder_name, subfolders, filenames in os.walk('C:\\delicious'):>>>     print('The current folder is {}'.format(folder_name))>>>>>>     for subfolder in subfolders:>>>         print('SUBFOLDER OF {}: {}'.format(folder_name, subfolder))>>>     for filename in filenames:>>>         print('FILE INSIDE {}: {}'.format(folder_name, filename))>>>>>>     print('')The current folder is C:\deliciousSUBFOLDER OF C:\delicious: catsSUBFOLDER OF C:\delicious: walnutFILE INSIDE C:\delicious: spam.txt​The current folder is C:\delicious\catsFILE INSIDE C:\delicious\cats: catnames.txtFILE INSIDE C:\delicious\cats: zophie.jpg​The current folder is C:\delicious\walnutSUBFOLDER OF C:\delicious\walnut: waffles​The current folder is C:\delicious\walnut\wafflesFILE INSIDE C:\delicious\walnut\waffles: butter.txt

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="f86105ada9544da9b03568d68693def5"><span data-offset-key="f86105ada9544da9b03568d68693def5:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="0704f418f50442a1b025854284146943"><span data-offset-key="0704f418f50442a1b025854284146943:0">`pathlib`</span><span data-offset-key="0704f418f50442a1b025854284146943:1"> provides a lot more functionality than the ones listed above, like getting file name, getting file extension, reading/writing a file without manually opening it, etc. Check out the </span></span><a href="https://docs.python.org/3/library/pathlib.html" class="link-a079aa82--primary-53a25e66--link-faf6c434"><span data-key="e2bce5f353434d5e9dc96cfd2887f696"><span data-offset-key="e2bce5f353434d5e9dc96cfd2887f696:0">official documentation</span></span></a><span data-key="5e018554d67944459331b6a281ce61dc"><span data-offset-key="5e018554d67944459331b6a281ce61dc:0"> if you want to know more!</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH600-23f228db--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="8e60cc5cc24a4bb4b22bb453c65acd5b"><span data-offset-key="8e60cc5cc24a4bb4b22bb453c65acd5b:0">Reading and Writing Files</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d5eec3f5b51a4b058867c198979639f2"><span data-offset-key="d5eec3f5b51a4b058867c198979639f2:0">The File Reading/Writing Process</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="915ae8ca1c6a4d84b6ecce5735ac529a"><span data-offset-key="915ae8ca1c6a4d84b6ecce5735ac529a:0">To read/write to a file in Python, you will want to use the </span><span data-offset-key="915ae8ca1c6a4d84b6ecce5735ac529a:1">`with`</span><span data-offset-key="915ae8ca1c6a4d84b6ecce5735ac529a:2"> statement, which will close the file for you after you are done.</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="53e2862db5b740a196df11a8e6e09f11"><span data-offset-key="53e2862db5b740a196df11a8e6e09f11:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="3f84ecb028114e3cb0687ab5b6abad75"><span data-offset-key="3f84ecb028114e3cb0687ab5b6abad75:0">Opening and reading files with the open() function</span></span></span>

    >>> with open('C:\\Users\\your_home_folder\\hello.txt') as hello_file:...     hello_content = hello_file.read()>>> hello_content'Hello World!'​>>> # Alternatively, you can use the *readlines()* method to get a list of string values from the file, one string for each line of text:​>>> with open('sonnet29.txt') as sonnet_file:...     sonnet_file.readlines()[When, in disgrace with fortune and men's eyes,\n', ' I all alone beweep myoutcast state,\n', And trouble deaf heaven with my bootless cries,\n', Andlook upon myself and curse my fate,']​>>> # You can also iterate through the file line by line:>>> with open('sonnet29.txt') as sonnet_file:...     for line in sonnet_file: # note the new line character will be included in the line...         print(line, end='')​When, in disgrace with fortune and men's eyes,I all alone beweep my outcast state,And trouble deaf heaven with my bootless cries,And look upon myself and curse my fate,

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="c4902ce25c38486ab5b45117ec4a4e9b"><span data-offset-key="c4902ce25c38486ab5b45117ec4a4e9b:0">Writing to Files</span></span></span>

    >>> with open('bacon.txt', 'w') as bacon_file:...     bacon_file.write('Hello world!\n')13​>>> with open('bacon.txt', 'a') as bacon_file:...     bacon_file.write('Bacon is not a vegetable.')25​>>> with open('bacon.txt') as bacon_file:...     content = bacon_file.read()​>>> print(content)Hello world!Bacon is not a vegetable.

### 

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="17503e2b39ea47eca83ccb9b15ed5837"><span data-offset-key="17503e2b39ea47eca83ccb9b15ed5837:0">Saving Variables with the shelve Module</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="48266442f3934f50a867e44578ae7656"><span data-offset-key="48266442f3934f50a867e44578ae7656:0">To save variables:</span></span></span>

    >>> import shelve​>>> cats = ['Zophie', 'Pooka', 'Simon']>>> with shelve.open('mydata') as shelf_file:...     shelf_file['cats'] = cats

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="9123221f17684494b527957272ebcba5"><span data-offset-key="9123221f17684494b527957272ebcba5:0">To open and read variables:</span></span></span>

    >>> with shelve.open('mydata') as shelf_file:...     print(type(shelf_file))...     print(shelf_file['cats'])<class 'shelve.DbfilenameShelf'>['Zophie', 'Pooka', 'Simon']

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="ee54b305aef94c4c888e5b46ae704ecc"><span data-offset-key="ee54b305aef94c4c888e5b46ae704ecc:0">Just like dictionaries, shelf values have keys() and values() methods that will return list-like values of the keys and values in the shelf. Since these methods return list-like values instead of true lists, you should pass them to the list() function to get them in list form.</span></span></span>

    >>> with shelve.open('mydata') as shelf_file:...     print(list(shelf_file.keys()))...     print(list(shelf_file.values()))['cats'][['Zophie', 'Pooka', 'Simon']]

<span class="text-4505230f--TextH400-3033861f--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="d5aff434528547fbae8eef0805eea6bb"><span data-offset-key="d5aff434528547fbae8eef0805eea6bb:0">*Return to the Top*</span></span></span>

<span class="text-4505230f--HeadingH400-686c0942--textContentFamily-49a318e1"><span data-key="84d825aa12104d19bf01976e70d10c97"><span data-offset-key="84d825aa12104d19bf01976e70d10c97:0">Saving Variables with the pprint.pformat() Function</span></span></span>

    >>> import pprint​>>> cats = [{'name': 'Zophie', 'desc': 'chubby'}, {'name': 'Pooka', 'desc': 'fluffy'}]​>>> pprint.pformat(cats)"[{'desc': 'chubby', 'name': 'Zophie'}, {'desc': 'fluffy', 'name': 'Pooka'}]"​>>> with open('myCats.py', 'w') as file_obj:...     file_obj.write('cats = {}\n'.format(pprint.pformat(cats)))83
